 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;For 2018 and 2017, potential dilutive securities&#13;had an anti-dilutive effect and were not included in the calculation of diluted net loss per common share. Stock options and warrants&#13;excluded from the calculation of diluted EPS because their effect was anti-dilutive were 11,173,500 and 11,292,300 of December&amp;#160;31,&amp;#160;2018&#13;and 2017, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;&lt;u&gt;Stock-Based&#13;Compensation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Under FASB ASC 718-10-30-2, all share-based&#13;payments to employees, including grants of employee stock options, are to be recognized in the income statement based on their&#13;fair values. Pro forma disclosure is no longer an alternative. Amortization of the fair values of stock options issued for services&#13;and compensation totaled $310,731 and $574,851 for the years ended December&amp;#160;31,&amp;#160;2018 and&amp;#160;2017, respectively. The&#13;fair values of stock options were determined using the Black-Scholes options pricing model and an effective term of 6 to 6.5 years&#13;based on the weighted average of the vesting periods and the stated term of the option grants and the discount rate on 5 to 7 year&#13;U.S. Treasury securities at the grant date and are being amortized over the related implied service term, or vesting period.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Uncertain Tax Positions&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In accordance with ASC 740, &amp;#8220;Income&#13;Taxes&amp;#8221; (&amp;#8220;ASC 740&amp;#8221;), the Company recognizes the tax benefit from an uncertain tax position only if it is more&#13;likely than not that the tax position will be capable of withstanding examination by the taxing authorities based on the technical&#13;merits of the position. These standards prescribe a recognition threshold and measurement attribute for the financial statement&#13;recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. These standards also provide guidance&#13;on de-recognition, classification, interest and penalties, accounting in interim periods, disclosure, and transition.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Various taxing authorities can periodically&#13;audit the Company&amp;#8217;s income tax returns. These audits include questions regarding the Company&amp;#8217;s tax filing positions,&#13;including the timing and amount of deductions and the allocation of income to various tax jurisdictions. In evaluating the exposures&#13;connected with these various tax filing positions, including state and local taxes, the Company records allowances for probable&#13;exposures. A number of years may elapse before a particular matter, for which an allowance has been established, is audited and&#13;fully resolved. The Company has not yet undergone an examination by any taxing authorities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The assessment of the Company&amp;#8217;s tax&#13;position relies on the judgment of management to estimate the exposures associated with the Company&amp;#8217;s various filing positions.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;From time to time,&#13;new accounting pronouncements are issued by the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&amp;#34;FASB&amp;#34;) that are adopted by the&#13;Company as of the specified effective date. If not discussed, management believes that the impact of recently issued standards,&#13;which are not yet effective, will not have a material impact on the Company's financial statements upon adoption.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; background-color: white&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August, 2016, the FASB issued Accounting&#13;Standards Update (ASU) No. 2016-15, &lt;i&gt;Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230): Classification of Certain Cash Receipts and Cash Payments&#13;&lt;/i&gt;(a consensus of the Emerging Issues Task Force). This guidance provides guidance of eight specific cash flow issues. This amendment&#13;is effective for periods beginning after December 15, 2017, with early adoption permitted. The Company adopted this standard on&#13;January 1, 2018 and anticipates it will not have a material impact on its financial statements and related disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In November 2016, the FASB issued ASU No.&#13;2016-18, &lt;i&gt;Restricted Cash&lt;/i&gt;. This guidance standardizes the presentation of changes to restricted cash on the statement of&#13;cash flows by requiring that a statement of cash flows explain the change during the period in the total of cash, cash equivalents,&#13;and amount generally described as restricted cash or restricted cash equivalents. The provisions of this standard are effective&#13;for annual reporting periods, and interim reporting periods contained therein, beginning after December 15, 2017, and early adoption&#13;is permitted. The Company adopted this guidance effective January 1, 2018 and applied it retrospectively, and the standard did&#13;not have a material impact on the Company&amp;#8217;s combined financial statements and related disclosures&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In January 2017, the FASB issued ASU No.&#13;2017-01, &lt;i&gt;Business Combinations&lt;/i&gt; (Topic 805): Clarifying the Definition of a Business, which clarifies the definition of a&#13;business to provide guidance in evaluating whether transactions should be accounted for as acquisitions (or disposals) of assets&#13;or businesses. ASU 2017-01 provides a screen to determine when a set of assets is not a business, requiring that when substantially&#13;all fair value of gross assets acquired (or disposed of) is concentrated in a single identifiable asset or group of similar identifiable&#13;assets, the set of assets is not a business. A framework is provided to assist in evaluating whether both an input and a substantive&#13;process are present for the set to be a business. ASU 2017-01 is effective for periods beginning after December 15, 2017, including&#13;interim periods within those annual periods. No disclosures are required at transition and early adoption is permitted. The Company&#13;adopted this standard on January 1, 2018 and will apply this guidance to future business combinations.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2017, the FASB issued ASU No. 2017-09,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8212; Stock Compensation&lt;/i&gt; (Topic 718); Scope of Modification Accounting. The amendments in this ASU provide&#13;guidance that clarifies when changes to the terms or conditions of a share-based payment award must be accounted for as modifications.&#13;If the value, vesting conditions or classification of the award changes, modification accounting will apply. The guidance is effective&#13;for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2017 and interim periods within those fiscal years. The Company adopted this guidance&#13;effective January 1, 2018, and the standard did not have a material impact on the Company&amp;#8217;s combined financial statements&#13;and related disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In June 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-07,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8212; Stock Compensation&lt;/i&gt; (Topic 718) - Improvements to Nonemployee Share-Based Payment Accounting, which&#13;simplifies accounting for share-based payment transactions resulting for acquiring goods and services from nonemployees. ASU 2018-07&#13;is effective for fiscal years, and interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2019. Early adoption&#13;is permitted. The Company is currently evaluating ASU 2018-07 and its impact on its combined financial statements or disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-10,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Codification Improvements to Topic 842, Leases&lt;/i&gt;. The amendments in ASU 2018-10 provide additional clarification and implementation&#13;guidance on certain aspects of the previously issued ASU No. 2016-02, Leases (Topic 842) (&amp;#8220;ASU 2016-02&amp;#8221;) and have the&#13;same effective and transition requirements as ASU 2016-02. Upon the effective date, ASU 2018-10 will supersede the current lease&#13;guidance in ASC Topic 840, Leases. Under the new guidance, lessees will be required to recognize for all leases, with the exception&#13;of short-term leases, a lease liability, which is a lessee&amp;#8217;s obligation to make lease payments arising from a lease, measured&#13;on a discounted basis. Concurrently, lessees will be required to recognize a right-of-use asset, which is an asset that represents&#13;the lessee&amp;#8217;s right to use, or control the use of, a specified asset for the lease term. ASU 2018-10 is effective for private&#13;companies and emerging growth public companies for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2019, with&#13;early adoption permitted. The guidance is required to be applied using a modified retrospective transition approach for leases&#13;existing at, or entered into after, the beginning of the earliest comparative periods presented in the financial statements. The&#13;Company is currently assessing the impact this guidance will have on its combined financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-09,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Codification Improvements&lt;/i&gt;. These amendments provide clarifications and corrections to certain ASC subtopics including the&#13;following: Income Statement - Reporting Comprehensive Income &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 220-10), Debt - Modifications and Extinguishments&#13;(Topic 470-50), Distinguishing Liabilities from Equity &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 480-10), Compensation - Stock Compensation - Income&#13;Taxes (Topic 718-740), Business Combinations - Income Taxes (Topic 805-740), Derivatives and Hedging &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 815-10),&#13;and Fair Value Measurement &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 820-10). The majority of the amendments in ASU 2018-09 will be effective in annual&#13;periods beginning after December 15, 2019. The Company is currently evaluating and assessing the impact this guidance will have&#13;on its combined financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-11,&#13;&amp;#8220;Leases (Topic 842): &lt;i&gt;Targeted Improvements.&lt;/i&gt; The amendments in ASU 2018-11 related to transition relief on comparative&#13;reporting at adoption affect all entities with lease contracts that choose the additional transition method and separating components&#13;of a contract affect only lessors whose lease contracts qualify for the practical expedient. The amendments in ASU 2018-11 are&#13;effective for private companies and emerging growth public companies for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2019, and interim&#13;periods within those fiscal years. The Company is currently assessing the impact this guidance will have on its combined financial&#13;statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has determined that BRAC, following&#13;its IPO, is a variable interest entity (&amp;#8220;VIE&amp;#8221;) and that the Company is the primary beneficiary of the VIE. The Company&#13;determined that, due to the redemption feature associated with the IPO shares, that the IPO shareholders are indirectly protected&#13;from the operating expenses of BRAC and it has the power to direct the activities of BRAC through the date at which BRAC affords&#13;the stockholders the opportunity to vote to approve a proposed business combination. Therefore, these consolidated financial statements&#13;herein contain the operations of the BRAC from its inception on May 9, 2017. BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO shareholders are reflected in our&#13;Consolidated Financial Statements as a non-controlling interest. The non-controlling interest was recorded at fair value on October&#13;10, 2017, with an addition on October 18, 2017 as a result of the underwriters&amp;#8217; exercise of their over-allotment option.&#13;All significant inter-company transactions have been eliminated in the preparation of theses financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company recognizes deferred tax assets&#13;and liabilities based on differences between the financial reporting and tax basis of assets and liabilities using the enacted&#13;tax rates and laws that are expected to be in effect when the differences are expected to be recovered. The Company provides a&#13;valuation allowance for deferred tax assets for which it does not consider realization of such assets to be more likely than not.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Basic and Diluted Earnings (Loss) Per&#13;Share&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Basic earnings (loss) per share (&amp;#8220;EPS&amp;#8221;)&#13;are computed by dividing net income (the numerator) by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period&#13;(the denominator). Diluted EPS is computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares and potential&#13;common shares outstanding (if dilutive) during each period. Potential common shares include stock options, warrants and restricted&#13;stock. The number of potential common shares outstanding relating to stock options, warrants and restricted stock is computed using&#13;the treasury stock method.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;&lt;u&gt;Stock-Based&#13;Compensation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Uncertain Tax Positions&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In accordance with ASC 740, &amp;#8220;Income&#13;Taxes&amp;#8221; (&amp;#8220;ASC 740&amp;#8221;), the Company recognizes the tax benefit from an uncertain tax position only if it is more&#13;likely than not that the tax position will be capable of withstanding examination by the taxing authorities based on the technical&#13;merits of the position. These standards prescribe a recognition threshold and measurement attribute for the financial statement&#13;recognition and measurement of a tax position taken or expected to be taken in a tax return. These standards also provide guidance&#13;on de-recognition, classification, interest and penalties, accounting in interim periods, disclosure, and transition.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Various taxing authorities can periodically&#13;audit the Company&amp;#8217;s income tax returns. These audits include questions regarding the Company&amp;#8217;s tax filing positions,&#13;including the timing and amount of deductions and the allocation of income to various tax jurisdictions. In evaluating the exposures&#13;connected with these various tax filing positions, including state and local taxes, the Company records allowances for probable&#13;exposures. A number of years may elapse before a particular matter, for which an allowance has been established, is audited and&#13;fully resolved. The Company has not yet undergone an examination by any taxing authorities.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Recent Accounting Pronouncements&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;From time to time,&#13;new accounting pronouncements are issued by the Financial Accounting Standards Board (&amp;#34;FASB&amp;#34;) that are adopted by the&#13;Company as of the specified effective date. If not discussed, management believes that the impact of recently issued standards,&#13;which are not yet effective, will not have a material impact on the Company's financial statements upon adoption.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; background-color: white&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In August, 2016, the FASB issued Accounting&#13;Standards Update (ASU) No. 2016-15, &lt;i&gt;Statement of Cash Flows (Topic 230): Classification of Certain Cash Receipts and Cash Payments&#13;&lt;/i&gt;(a consensus of the Emerging Issues Task Force). This guidance provides guidance of eight specific cash flow issues. This amendment&#13;is effective for periods beginning after December 15, 2017, with early adoption permitted. The Company adopted this standard on&#13;January 1, 2018 and anticipates it will not have a material impact on its financial statements and related disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In November 2016, the FASB issued ASU No.&#13;2016-18, &lt;i&gt;Restricted Cash&lt;/i&gt;. This guidance standardizes the presentation of changes to restricted cash on the statement of&#13;cash flows by requiring that a statement of cash flows explain the change during the period in the total of cash, cash equivalents,&#13;and amount generally described as restricted cash or restricted cash equivalents. The provisions of this standard are effective&#13;for annual reporting periods, and interim reporting periods contained therein, beginning after December 15, 2017, and early adoption&#13;is permitted. The Company adopted this guidance effective January 1, 2018 and applied it retrospectively, and the standard did&#13;not have a material impact on the Company&amp;#8217;s combined financial statements and related disclosures&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In January 2017, the FASB issued ASU No.&#13;2017-01, &lt;i&gt;Business Combinations&lt;/i&gt; (Topic 805): Clarifying the Definition of a Business, which clarifies the definition of a&#13;business to provide guidance in evaluating whether transactions should be accounted for as acquisitions (or disposals) of assets&#13;or businesses. ASU 2017-01 provides a screen to determine when a set of assets is not a business, requiring that when substantially&#13;all fair value of gross assets acquired (or disposed of) is concentrated in a single identifiable asset or group of similar identifiable&#13;assets, the set of assets is not a business. A framework is provided to assist in evaluating whether both an input and a substantive&#13;process are present for the set to be a business. ASU 2017-01 is effective for periods beginning after December 15, 2017, including&#13;interim periods within those annual periods. No disclosures are required at transition and early adoption is permitted. The Company&#13;adopted this standard on January 1, 2018 and will apply this guidance to future business combinations.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In May 2017, the FASB issued ASU No. 2017-09,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8212; Stock Compensation&lt;/i&gt; (Topic 718); Scope of Modification Accounting. The amendments in this ASU provide&#13;guidance that clarifies when changes to the terms or conditions of a share-based payment award must be accounted for as modifications.&#13;If the value, vesting conditions or classification of the award changes, modification accounting will apply. The guidance is effective&#13;for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2017 and interim periods within those fiscal years. The Company adopted this guidance&#13;effective January 1, 2018, and the standard did not have a material impact on the Company&amp;#8217;s combined financial statements&#13;and related disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In June 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-07,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Compensation &amp;#8212; Stock Compensation&lt;/i&gt; (Topic 718) - Improvements to Nonemployee Share-Based Payment Accounting, which&#13;simplifies accounting for share-based payment transactions resulting for acquiring goods and services from nonemployees. ASU 2018-07&#13;is effective for fiscal years, and interim periods within those fiscal years, beginning after December 15, 2019. Early adoption&#13;is permitted. The Company is currently evaluating ASU 2018-07 and its impact on its combined financial statements or disclosures.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-10,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Codification Improvements to Topic 842, Leases&lt;/i&gt;. The amendments in ASU 2018-10 provide additional clarification and implementation&#13;guidance on certain aspects of the previously issued ASU No. 2016-02, Leases (Topic 842) (&amp;#8220;ASU 2016-02&amp;#8221;) and have the&#13;same effective and transition requirements as ASU 2016-02. Upon the effective date, ASU 2018-10 will supersede the current lease&#13;guidance in ASC Topic 840, Leases. Under the new guidance, lessees will be required to recognize for all leases, with the exception&#13;of short-term leases, a lease liability, which is a lessee&amp;#8217;s obligation to make lease payments arising from a lease, measured&#13;on a discounted basis. Concurrently, lessees will be required to recognize a right-of-use asset, which is an asset that represents&#13;the lessee&amp;#8217;s right to use, or control the use of, a specified asset for the lease term. ASU 2018-10 is effective for private&#13;companies and emerging growth public companies for interim and annual reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2019, with&#13;early adoption permitted. The guidance is required to be applied using a modified retrospective transition approach for leases&#13;existing at, or entered into after, the beginning of the earliest comparative periods presented in the financial statements. The&#13;Company is currently assessing the impact this guidance will have on its combined financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-09,&#13;&lt;i&gt;Codification Improvements&lt;/i&gt;. These amendments provide clarifications and corrections to certain ASC subtopics including the&#13;following: Income Statement - Reporting Comprehensive Income &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 220-10), Debt - Modifications and Extinguishments&#13;(Topic 470-50), Distinguishing Liabilities from Equity &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 480-10), Compensation - Stock Compensation - Income&#13;Taxes (Topic 718-740), Business Combinations - Income Taxes (Topic 805-740), Derivatives and Hedging &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 815-10),&#13;and Fair Value Measurement &amp;#8211; Overall (Topic 820-10). The majority of the amendments in ASU 2018-09 will be effective in annual&#13;periods beginning after December 15, 2019. The Company is currently evaluating and assessing the impact this guidance will have&#13;on its combined financial statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In July 2018, the FASB issued ASU No. 2018-11,&#13;&amp;#8220;Leases (Topic 842): &lt;i&gt;Targeted Improvements.&lt;/i&gt; The amendments in ASU 2018-11 related to transition relief on comparative&#13;reporting at adoption affect all entities with lease contracts that choose the additional transition method and separating components&#13;of a contract affect only lessors whose lease contracts qualify for the practical expedient. The amendments in ASU 2018-11 are&#13;effective for private companies and emerging growth public companies for fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2019, and interim&#13;periods within those fiscal years. The Company is currently assessing the impact this guidance will have on its combined financial&#13;statements.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 3 &amp;#8211; Going Concern&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;As shown in the accompanying financial&#13;statements, as of December 31, 2018 the Company had a cash balance of $1,503,500 and total working capital of $898,097 The Company&#13;has no revenue source presently. Based on projections of cash expenditures in the Company&amp;#8217;s current business plan, the cash&#13;on hand would be insufficient to fund the Company&amp;#8217;s general and administrative expenses over the next year.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company continues to pursue sources&#13;of additional capital through various management fee agreements and financing transactions or arrangements, including joint venturing&#13;of projects, equity financing or other means. We may not be successful in identifying suitable funding transactions in a sufficient&#13;time period or at all, and we may not obtain the capital we require by other means. If we do not succeed in raising additional&#13;capital, our resources may not be sufficient to fund our business.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 4 &amp;#8211; Rights Offering and Formation&#13;of Black Ridge Acquisition Corp.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;The Company filed a Registration Statement&#13;on Form S-1 (the &amp;#8220;Registration Statement&amp;#8221;) with the SEC to register the issuance of 431,819,910 shares of common stock&#13;in the Rights Offering that was declared effective by the SEC on August 3, 2017. Pursuant to the Rights Offering, the Company distributed,&#13;on a pro rata basis, one right for each share of common stock owned by shareholders on August 2, 2017 (the &amp;#8220;Record Date&amp;#8221;).&#13;Each right permitted a shareholder to purchase up to nine shares of common stock at a subscription price of $0.012 per share. The&#13;Rights Offering expired on September 8, 2017 (the &amp;#8220;Expiration Date&amp;#8221;).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;In connection with the Rights Offering,&#13;the Company also entered into a Standby Purchase Agreement (the &amp;#8220;Backstop Agreement&amp;#8221;) with a consortium of investors,&#13;including members of the Company&amp;#8217;s board of directors and our Chief Executive Officer (collectively, the &amp;#8220;Backstop&#13;Purchasers&amp;#8221;), who agree to purchase up to $2.9 million of the unsubscribed shares following the completion of the rights&#13;offering.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;On September 26, 2017, the Company completed&#13;the Rights Offering, raising gross proceeds of $5,181,839 and issued 431,819,910 shares in connection with the exercise of rights&#13;in connection with the Rights Offering and related Backstop Agreement. Under the Rights Offering the Company&amp;#8217;s current shareholders&#13;exercised rights to purchase 199,811,421 shares of stock for a total of $2,397,737. Under the Backstop Agreement, the Backstop&#13;Purchasers purchased 232,008,489 shares of stock for a total of $2,784,102. Officers and directors of the Company purchased 173,843,308&#13;shares between the Rights Offering and as participants of the Backstop Agreement for $2,086,120 and received 179,376 warrants to&#13;purchase shares of common stock at $0.01 per share for their participation in the Backstop Agreement. The remaining 257,976,602&#13;shares were purchased by non-related parties for proceeds of $2,965,555. The warrants issued to related parties fair value was estimated&#13;to be $4,179 (see Note 15). The Company incurred $130,164 in costs associated with raising capital, which has been netted against&#13;stockholders&amp;#8217; equity. Additionally as part of Backstop agreement, the Company issued 435,000 warrants to purchase its common&#13;stock at $0.01 for participants in the Backstop Agreement. The warrants fair value was estimated to be $10,135 (see Note 15).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 5 &amp;#8211; BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO, Consolidation&#13;of BRAC and Non-controlling Interest&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The registration statement for the BRAC&amp;#8217;s&#13;IPO was declared effective on October 4, 2017. The registration statement was initially declared effective for 10,000,000 units&#13;(&amp;#8220;Units&amp;#8221; and, with respect to the common stock included in the Units being offered, the &amp;#8220;Public Shares&amp;#8221;),&#13;but the offering was increased to 12,000,000 Units pursuant to Rule 462(b) under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended. On October&#13;10, 2017, the Company consummated the Initial Public Offering of 12,000,000 units, generating gross proceeds of $120,000,000.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Simultaneous with the closing of the Initial&#13;Public Offering, BRAC sold 400,000 units (the &amp;#8220;Placement Units&amp;#8221;) at a price of $10.00 per Unit in a private placement&#13;to BROG, generating gross proceeds of $4,000,000. BROG&amp;#8217;s investment in BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock is eliminated in consolidation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Transaction costs relating to the IPO amounted&#13;to $2,882,226, consisting of $2,400,000 of underwriting fees and $482,226 of other costs.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Following the closing of the IPO on October&#13;10, 2017, an amount of $120,600,000 ($10.05 per Unit) from the net proceeds of the sale of the Units in the IPO and the Placement&#13;Units was placed in a trust account (&amp;#8220;Trust Account&amp;#8221;) and is invested in U.S. government securities, within the meaning&#13;set forth in Section 2(a)(16) of the Investment Company Act of 1940, as amended (the &amp;#8220;Investment Company Act&amp;#8221;), with&#13;a maturity of 180 days or less or in any open-ended investment company that holds itself out as a money market fund selected by&#13;the Company meeting the conditions of paragraphs (d)(2), (d)(3) and (d)(4) of Rule 2a-7 of the Investment Company Act, as determined&#13;by the Company, until the earlier of: (i) the consummation of a Business Combination or (ii) the distribution of the Trust Account,&#13;as described below.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On October 18, 2017, in connection with&#13;the underwriters&amp;#8217; exercise of their over-allotment option in full, BRAC sold an additional 1,800,000 Units and the sale&#13;of an additional 45,000 Placement Units to BROG at $10.00 per Unit, generating total proceeds of $18,450,000. Transaction costs&#13;for underwriting fees on the sale of the over-allotment units were $360,000. Following the closing, an additional $18,090,000&#13;of the net proceeds ($10.05 per Unit) was placed in the Trust Account, bringing the total aggregate proceeds held in the Trust&#13;Account to $138,690,000 ($10.05 per Unit). BROG&amp;#8217;s investment in BRAC&amp;#8217;s common stock is eliminated in consolidation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;BRAC&amp;#8217;s&#13;management has broad discretion with respect to the specific application of the net proceeds of the IPO and private placement,&#13;although substantially all of the net proceeds are intended to be applied generally toward consummating a Business Combination.&#13;There is no assurance that the BRAC will be able to complete a Business Combination successfully. Upon the closing of the IPO,&#13;$10.05 per Unit sold in the IPO, including some of the proceeds of the Private Placements was deposited in a trust account (&amp;#8220;Trust&#13;Account&amp;#8221;) to be held until the earlier of (i) the consummation of its initial Business Combination or (ii) BRAC&amp;#8217;s&#13;failure to consummate a Business Combination within 21 months from the consummation of the IPO (the &amp;#8220;Combination Period&amp;#8221;).&#13;Placing funds in the Trust Account may not protect those funds from third party claims against BRAC. Although BRAC will seek to&#13;have all vendors, service providers, prospective target businesses or other entities it engages, execute agreements with BRAC&#13;waiving any claim of any kind in or to any monies held in the Trust Account, there is no guarantee that such persons will execute&#13;such agreements. The Trust Account is maintained by a third party trustee. The remaining net proceeds (not held in the Trust Account)&#13;may be used to pay for business, legal and accounting due diligence on prospective acquisitions and continuing general and administrative&#13;expenses. Additionally, the interest earned on the Trust Account balance may be released to BRAC for any amounts that are necessary&#13;to pay BRAC&amp;#8217;s income and other tax obligations and up to $50,000 that may be used to pay for the costs of liquidating BRAC.&#13;BROG has agreed that it will be liable to ensure that the proceeds in the Trust Account are not reduced below $10.05 per share&#13;by the claims of target businesses or claims of vendors or other entities that are owed money by BRAC for services rendered or&#13;contracted for or products sold to BRAC, but there is no assurance that BROG will be able to satisfy its indemnification obligations&#13;if it is required to do so. Additionally, the agreement entered into by BROG specifically provides for two exceptions to the indemnity&#13;it has given: it will have no liability (1) as to any claimed amounts owed to a target business or vendor or other entity who&#13;has executed an agreement with BRAC waiving any right, title, interest or claim of any kind they may have in or to any monies&#13;held in the Trust Account, or (2) as to any claims for indemnification by the underwriters of the IPO against certain liabilities,&#13;including liabilities under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Initial Business Combination&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Pursuant to the Nasdaq Capital Markets&#13;listing rules, BRAC&amp;#8217;s initial Business Combination must be with a target business or businesses whose collective fair market&#13;value is at least equal to 80% of the balance in the Trust Account at the time of the execution of a definitive agreement for such&#13;Business Combination, although this may entail simultaneous acquisitions of several target businesses. The fair market value of&#13;the target will be determined by BRAC&amp;#8217;s board of directors based upon one or more standards generally accepted by the financial&#13;community (such as actual and potential sales, earnings, cash flow and/or book value). The target business or businesses that BRAC&#13;acquires may have a collective fair market value substantially in excess of 80% of the Trust Account balance. In order to consummate&#13;such a Business Combination, BRAC may issue a significant amount of its debt or equity securities to the sellers of such business&#13;and/or seek to raise additional funds through a private offering of debt or equity securities. If BRAC&amp;#8217;s securities are not&#13;listed on NASDAQ after the IPO, BRAC would not be required to satisfy the 80% requirement. However, BRAC intends to satisfy the&#13;80% requirement even if BRAC&amp;#8217;s securities are not listed on NASDAQ at the time of the initial Business Combination.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;BRAC will provide the public stockholders,&#13;who are the holders of the common stock which was sold as part of the Units in the IPO, whether they are purchased in the IPO or&#13;in the aftermarket, or &amp;#8220;Public Shares&amp;#8221;, including BROG to the extent that it purchases such Public Shares (&amp;#8220;Public&#13;Stockholders&amp;#8221;), with an opportunity to redeem all or a portion of their Public Shares of BRAC&amp;#8217;s Common stock, irrespective&#13;of whether they vote for or against the proposed transaction or if BRAC conducts a tender offer, upon the completion of the initial&#13;Business Combination either (1) in connection with a stockholder meeting called to approve the Business Combination, or (ii) by&#13;means of a tender offer, at a per-share price, payable in cash, equal to the aggregate amount then on deposit in the Trust Account&#13;including interest (net of franchise and income taxes payable, divided by the number of then outstanding Public Shares. The amount&#13;in the Trust Account, net of franchise and income taxes payable, currently amounts to $10.06 per Public Share. The common stock&#13;subject to redemption will be recorded at a redemption value and classified a temporary equity upon the completion of the IPO,&#13;in accordance with Accounting Standards Codification (&amp;#8220;ASC&amp;#8221;) Topic 480 &amp;#8220;Distinguishing Liabilities from Equity&amp;#8221;.&#13;BRAC will proceed with a Business Combination only if BRAC has net tangible assets of at least $5,000,001 upon such consummation&#13;of a Business Combination and in the case of a stockholder vote, a majority of the outstanding shares voted are voted in favor&#13;of the Business Combination. The decision as to whether BRAC will seek stockholder approval of a proposed Business Combination&#13;or conduct a tender offer will be made by BRAC, solely in its discretion, based on a variety of factors such as the timing of the&#13;transaction and whether the terms of the transaction would otherwise require it to seek stockholder approval under the law or stock&#13;exchange listing requirement. If a stockholder vote is not required and BRAC decides not to hold a stockholder vote for business&#13;or other legal reasons, BRAC will, pursuant to the proposed amended and restated certificate of incorporation, (i) conduct the&#13;redemptions pursuant to Rule 13e-4 and Regulation 14E of the Exchange Act, which regulate issuer tender offers, and (ii) file tender&#13;offer documents with the SEC prior to completing the initial Business Combination which contain substantially the same financial&#13;and other information about the initial Business Combination and the redemption rights as is required under Regulation 14A of the&#13;Exchange Act, which regulates the solicitation of proxies.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;BROG has agreed to vote its Founder Shares&#13;and any Public Shares purchased during or after the IPO in favor of the initial Business Combination, and BRAC&amp;#8217;s executive&#13;officers and directors have also agreed to vote any Public Shares purchased during or after the IPO in favor of the Initial Business&#13;Combination. BROG entered into a letter agreement, pursuant to which it agreed to waive its redemption rights with respect to the&#13;Founder Shares, shares included in the Placement Units and Public Shares in connection with the completion of the initial Business&#13;Combination. In addition, BROG has agreed to waive its rights to liquidating distributions from the Trust Account with respect&#13;to the Founder Shares and shares included in the Placement Units if BRAC fails to complete the initial Business Combination within&#13;the prescribed time frame. However, if BROG (or any of BRAC&amp;#8217;s executive officers, directors or affiliates) acquires Public&#13;Shares in or after the IPO, it will be entitled to liquidating distributions from the Trust Account with respect to such Public&#13;Shares in the event BRAC does not complete the initial Business Combination within such applicable time period.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif&gt;&lt;i&gt;Proposed Business Combination&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify; text-indent: 15pt&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On December 19, 2018,&#13;BRAC entered into a business combination agreement (the &amp;#8220;Business Combination Agreement&amp;#8221;) with Allied Esports Entertainment,&#13;Inc. (&amp;#8220;Allied Esports&amp;#8221;), Ourgame International Holdings Ltd. (&amp;#8220;Ourgame&amp;#8221;), Noble Link Global Limited, a&#13;wholly-owned subsidiary of Ourgame (&amp;#8220;Noble&amp;#8221;), and Primo Vital Ltd., also a wholly-owned subsidiary of Ourgame (&amp;#8220;Primo&amp;#8221;),&#13;pursuant to which BRAC will acquire two of Ourgame&amp;#8217;s global esports and entertainment assets, Allied Esports and WPT Enterprises,&#13;Inc. (&amp;#8220;WPT&amp;#8221;) . See Note 19.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0.5in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Failure to Consummate a Business Combination&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;If BRAC is unable to complete the initial&#13;Business Combination within the Combination Period, BRAC must: (i) cease all operations except for the purpose of winding up, (ii)&#13;as promptly as reasonably possible but not more than ten business days thereafter, redeem the public shares, at a per-share price,&#13;payable in cash, equal to the aggregate amount then on deposit in the Trust Account, including interest (which interest shall be&#13;net of franchise and income taxes payable divided by the number of then outstanding Public Shares, which redemption will completely&#13;extinguish Public Stockholders&amp;#8217; rights as stockholders (including the right to receive further liquidation distributions,&#13;if any), subject to applicable law, and (iii) as promptly as reasonably possible following such redemption, subject to the approval&#13;of BRAC&amp;#8217;s remaining stockholders and BRAC&amp;#8217;s Board of Directors, dissolve and liquidate, subject in the case of clauses&#13;(ii) and (iii) to BRAC&amp;#8217;s obligations under Delaware law to provide for claims of creditors and the requirements of other&#13;applicable law.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Consolidation of BRAC and Non-controlling&#13;Interest&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has determined that BRAC, following&#13;its IPO, is a variable interest entity (&amp;#8220;VIE&amp;#8221;) and that the Company is the primary beneficiary of the VIE. The Company&#13;determined that, due to the redemption feature associated with the IPO shares, that the IPO shareholders are indirectly protected&#13;from the operating expenses of BRAC and BROG has the power to direct the activities of BRAC through the date at which BRAC affords&#13;the stockholders the opportunity to vote to approve a proposed business combination. Therefore, these consolidated financial statements&#13;contain the operations of the BRAC from its inception on May 9, 2017. BRAC&amp;#8217;s IPO shareholders are reflected in our Consolidated&#13;Financial Statements as a redeemable non-controlling interest. The non-controlling interest was recorded at fair value on October&#13;10, 2017, with an addition on October 18, 2017 as a result of the underwriters&amp;#8217; exercise of their over-allotment option.&#13;The net earnings attributable to the IPO shareholders are subtracted from the net loss for the year ended December 31, 2017 to&#13;arrive at the net loss attributable to the Company and the non-controlling interest on the balance sheet was adjusted to include&#13;the net earnings attributable to the IPO shareholders.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;i&gt;Intercompany transactions and eliminations&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;BROG is paid a management fee by BRAC of&#13;$10,000 per month as part of an administrative services agreement, which commenced October 5, 2017, for general and administrative&#13;services including the cost of office space and personnel dedicated to BRAC. BROG is reimbursed for any out-of-pocket expenses,&#13;particularly travel, incurred in connection with activities on BRAC&amp;#8217;s behalf, including but not limited to identifying potential&#13;target businesses and performing due diligence on suitable business combinations. There is no cap or ceiling on the reimbursement&#13;of out-of-pocket expenses incurred by BRAC. BRAC paid a total of $28,710 to BROG for such services during the year ended December&#13;31, 2017. The management services income of BROG and the management services expense of BRAC as well as any balances due between&#13;the companies for such services or reimbursements were eliminated in consolidation.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 8 &amp;#8211; Related Party&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;As described in Note&#13;4, officers and directors of the Company purchased 173,843,308 shares between the Rights Offering and as participants of the Backstop&#13;Agreement for $2,086,120 and received 179,376 warrants to purchase shares of common stock at $0.01 per share for their participation&#13;in the Backstop Agreement.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On March 1, 2018, the Board of Directors&#13;(the &amp;#8220;Board&amp;#8221;) of the Company approved and adopted the Black Ridge Gas, Inc. 2018 Management Incentive Plan (the &amp;#8220;Plan&amp;#8221;)&#13;and the form of 2018 Management Incentive Plan Award Agreement (the &amp;#8220;Award Agreement&amp;#8221;).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&lt;u&gt;BRAC Loan&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;In order to finance transaction costs in&#13;connection with an intended initial business combination, BROG, and its officers, directors or their affiliates may, but are not&#13;obligated to, loan BRAC funds as may be required. If BRAC consummates an initial business combination, BRAC would repay such loaned&#13;amounts. In the event that the initial business combination does not close, BRAC may use a portion of the working capital held&#13;outside the trust account to repay such loaned amounts, but no proceeds from BRAC&amp;#8217;s trust account would be used for such&#13;repayment. Up to $1,500,000 of such loans may be convertible into units of the post business combination entity at a price of $10.00&#13;per unit at the option of the lender. The units would be identical to the Placement Units.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

   &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 2.5pt double; text-align: left&gt;$&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 2.5pt double; text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;/table&gt;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note 11 &amp;#8211; Fair Value of Financial&#13;Instruments&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;Under FASB ASC 820-10-5, fair value is&#13;defined as the price that would be received to sell an asset or paid to transfer a liability in an orderly transaction between&#13;market participants at the measurement date (an exit price). The standard outlines a valuation framework and creates a fair value&#13;hierarchy in order to increase the consistency and comparability of fair value measurements and the related disclosures. Under&#13;GAAP, certain assets and liabilities must be measured at fair value, and FASB ASC 820-10-50 details the disclosures that are required&#13;for items measured at fair value.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has cash and cash equivalents&#13;and a revolving credit facility that must be measured under the fair value standard. The Company&amp;#8217;s financial assets and liabilities&#13;are measured using inputs from the three levels of the fair value hierarchy. The three levels are as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 40pt; text-align: justify&gt;Level 1 - Inputs are unadjusted&#13;quoted prices in active markets for identical assets or liabilities that the Company has the ability to access at the measurement&#13;date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 40pt; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 40pt; text-align: justify&gt;Level 2 - Inputs include quoted&#13;prices for similar assets and liabilities in active markets, quoted prices for identical or similar assets or liabilities in markets&#13;that are not active, inputs other than quoted prices that are observable for the asset or liability (e.g., interest rates, yield&#13;curves, etc.), and inputs that are derived principally from or corroborated by observable market data by correlation or other means&#13;(market corroborated inputs).&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0 0pt 40pt; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;&lt;u&gt;Preferred Stock&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has 20,000,000 authorized shares&#13;of $0.001 par value preferred stock. No shares have been issued to date.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify; background-color: white&gt;&lt;u&gt;Common Stock&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;The Company has 500,000,000 authorized&#13;shares of $0.001 par value common stock.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=margin: 0pt 0; font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;On September 26, 2017 the Company issued&#13;199,811,421 shares of common stock in a Rights Offering, raising gross proceeds of $2,397,737, and issued an additional 232,008,789&#13;shares in a private placement (the Backstop Agreement), raising gross proceeds of $2,784,102. The Company incurred $130,164 in&#13;costs associated with the Rights Offering and Backstop Agreement.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Options Cancelled&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the years ended December 31, 2018&#13;and 2017, 61,800 and 87,700 options, respectively, were forfeited by a former employee.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Options Expired&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;During the years ended December 31, 2018,&#13;and 2017, 12,000 and 12,000 options, respectively, with a strike price of $0.08 per share and $0.29 per share, respectively, expired.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0&gt;&lt;u&gt;Warrants Granted&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman

 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;No warrants were granted during the year&#13;ended December&amp;#160;31, 2018.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;The Company issued 435,000 warrants to&#13;purchase shares at $0.01 per share to participants of the Backstop Agreement on September 22, 2017. The Company accounted for the&#13;warrants as an expense of the Rights Offering which resulted in a charge directly to stockholders&amp;#8217; equity. The Company estimated&#13;the fair value of these warrants to be approximately $10,135 (or $.0233 per warrant) using the Black-Scholes option-pricing model.&#13;The fair value of the warrants was estimated as of the date of grant using the following assumptions: (1) expected volatility of&#13;388%, (2) risk-free interest rate of 1.89% and (3) expected life of five years.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Warrants Cancelled&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;No warrants were cancelled during the years&#13;ended December&amp;#160;31, 2018 and 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Warrants Expired&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;No warrants were expired during the years&#13;ended December&amp;#160;31, 2018 and 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&lt;u&gt;Warrants Exercised&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;45,000 warrants were exercised during the&#13;year ended December 31, 2018 for $.01 per share resulting in proceeds of $450.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;No warrants were exercised during the year&#13;ended December&amp;#160;31, 2017.&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times
 Serif; margin: 0pt 0; text-align: justify&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/p&gt;&#13;&#13;&lt;p style=font: 10pt Times New Roman
 Times

204)&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;Warrants expired&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: White&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;Warrants cancelled&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: rgb(204

204)&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;Warrants granted&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: right&gt;&amp;#8211;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: White&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: justify&gt;Warrants exercised&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: right&gt;(45,000&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;)&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=border-bottom: Black 1pt solid; text-align: right&gt;0.01&lt;/td&gt;&#13;    &lt;td style=text-align: left&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&#13;&lt;tr style=vertical-align: bottom; background-color: rgb(204
